Jamison Brereton

108 (820)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Gauriv─лti ┼Ъ─Бktya 1тАУ2, ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 3, 14тАУ16, ┼кru ─Ас╣Еgirasa 4тАУ5, R╠еji┼Ыvan Bh─Бradv─Бja 6тАУ7, ┼кrdhvasadman ─Ас╣Еgirasa 8тАУ9, Krtaya ╠е ┼Ыas ─Ас╣Еgirasa 10тАУ11, R╠ес╣Зaс╣Гcaya 12тАУ13 16 verses: kakubh alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, except g─Бyatr─л yavamadhy─Б 13, arranged in prag─Бthas
The Anukramaс╣З─л names seven different poets as authors of this hymn; the Anukramaс╣З─лтАЩs divisions do not correspond at all to the clear prag─Бtha structure, however, and therefore seem questionable. Within the prag─Бthas there is, more often than not, syntactic dependency between verses (e.g., vss. 3тАУ4, 7тАУ8, 13тАУ14), as well as some thematic continuity. Stylistically the hymn, especially toward the beginning, is characterized by rather choppy syntax and often presents itself as a mosaic of semi self-contained phrases. On the other hand, there are signs of ring composition: the first phrase of the hymn, тАЬpurify yourself as the most honeyed for Indra, o SomaтАЭ recurs as the framing words of the first verse of the final prag─Бtha (vs. 15), and the relative clause about the drinking of soma that introduces verse 2 is echoed, with the same relative pronoun, in 14a.
Allusions to the Vala myth are found in the interior of the hymn (vss. 4, 6). The heavenly soma, conceived of in part as rain, is also a prominent theme (vss. 9тАУ11, and also probably vss. 4 [the тАЬdear immortal oneтАЭ] and 6 [the тАЬwateryтАЭ cows]). This cosmic soma is, as usual, a counterpoint to the ritual soma, the standard details of whose preparation are found throughout.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the structure of the hymn see published introduction. It consists of prag─Бthas alternating Kakubh (8 12 / 8) with Satobс╣Ыhat─л (12 8 / 12 8). The Anukr. attributes the hymn to seven different poets, but the vss. assigned to them generally violate the prag─Бtha division, which, as the published introduction. indicates, is often reinforced by syntactic structure. The Anukr. also identifies vs. 13 as G─Бyatr─л Yavamadhy─Б, but it can be analyzed as a reasonably well-behaved Kakubh.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSoma,who are most sweet-flavoured, most intelligent, the exhilarator, flow for Indra, the great, the most brilliant,the exhilarator.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself as the most honeyed for Indra, o Soma, as the
exhilarating drink that best finds resolve,
greatly, as the exhilarating drink that best rules heaven, с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is syntactic dependence between the two vss., at least by my reading: 2ab depends on vs. 1, while 2cd consists of a new cl., with a change of person. The Anukr. attributes the two vss. to Gauriv─лti ┼Ъ─Бktya; there is some support for this, in that V.29 (one of the three other hymns attributed to him [also X.73-74]) has an allusion to the myth involving Eta┼Ыa, the sunтАЩs horse (V.29.5), who appears in our 2d.

Griffith

FOR Indra, flow thou Soma on, as gladdening juice most sweet, intelligent,
Great, cheering, dwelling most in heaven.

Geldner

L├дutere dich, Soma, f├╝r Indra als s├╝├Яester, am besten ratfindender Rauschtrank, als weitaus der himmlischste Rauschtrank;

Grassmann

Dem Indra str├╢m, o Soma, hell, als s├╝ssestes, als kraftverleihendstes Getr├дnk, erhaben himmlisches Getr├дnk.

Elizarenkova

рд╡реГрд╖рднрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдХ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдпрд╕реНрдп рдпрдВ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдкреАрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛рдпрддреЗ рд╡реГрд╖рдн рдЗрд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрджреГрд╢рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рджрд░реНрд╢рдХрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрдп рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдкреАрддрд╛ рдкрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдХреЗрддрдГ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рд╕рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЗрд╖рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдордиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрднреНрдпрдХреНрд░рдореАрддреН рдЕрднрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдорддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГред рд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рдиреИрддрд╢рдГ ред рдПрддрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рдирд╛рдо ред рдпрдерд╛рд╢реНрд╡реЛ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордорднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy drinking whom the showerer Indra is invigorated, by drinking you who are the beholder of everything, the intelligent (Indra) reaches the viands (of the enemy) as a horse (reaches) the battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Since, having drunk of you, the bull acts as a bull, at the drinking of this sun-finding (soma).
Bearing good marks he [=Soma] strode toward the refreshments, like Eta┼Ыa toward the prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. presents us with a syntactic trap of sorts. It appears to consist of a standard REL / COREL construction, with 2a beginning y├бsya te and 2c beg. s├б. And indeed the rel. and the s├б are coreferential; however, the grammatical person has changed from 2nd to 3rd. I therefore prefer (contra Geldner/Renou) to attach 2ab to the previous vs., in which Soma is also 2nd ps. P─Бda b acts as a transition from Soma as 2nd ps. to Soma as 3rd ps., with asy├б referring to him, but the parallelism between the two тАЬdrinkingтАЭ expressions keeps it within the syntactic domain of the rel. clause.

I have silently converted y├бsya into y├бd, since тАЬupon drinking of which - of you –тАЭ is unparsable, or at least exceptionally awk., in English.

The gerund p─лtv─Б╠Бin a is echoed by the i-stem loc. p─лt─Б╠Бin b.

On the unexpected accent of supr├бketa-, as opposed to supraket├б- (4x), see Oldenberg, who has no good explanation (nor do I).

01-02 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

There is syntactic dependence between the two vss., at least by my reading: 2ab depends on vs. 1, while 2cd consists of a new cl., with a change of person. The Anukr. attributes the two vss. to Gauriv─лti ┼Ъ─Бktya; there is some support for this, in that V.29 (one of the three other hymns attributed to him [also X.73-74]) has an allusion to the myth involving Eta┼Ыa, the sunтАЩs horse (V.29.5), who appears in our 2d.

Griffith

Thou, of whom having drunk the Steer acts like a steer. drinking of this that finds the light,
He, Excellently Wise, is come to strengthening food, to spoil and wealth like Etasa.

Geldner

Du, nach dessen Trunke der Bulle sich als Bulle f├╝hlt, bei dem Trunke dieses Sonnen-finders, dieser Soma ist unter guten Vorzeichen auf die Speisegen├╝sse losgegangen wie Etasa auf den Kampfpreis.

Grassmann

Nach dessen Trunk der Stier sich als ein Stier erweist, zu dieses Segenspenders Trunk Hat sich den Tr├дnken nun genaht der herrliche, wie zu dem Preis das schnelle Ross.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(You) through whom Dadhya├▒c tthe offerer of the nine days’ rites opened (the cave), through whom the с╣Ыс╣гis recovered (the stolen cows), through whom under the protection of the gods the worshippers obtained the sustenance of the delicious (ambrosial water).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With whom Navagva, with whom Dadhya├▒c uncloses (the cowpen), by whom the inspired poets have acquired for themselves
(some) of the dear immortal one [=heavenly soma] in the grace of the gods, by whom they have each attained fame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although p─Бda a treats the mythological pastтАФthe opening of the Vala cave (Navagva) and Dadhya├▒cтАЩs presumably similar exploit (see his connection with cow pens in X.48.2)тАФthe verb is present tense aporс╣Зut├й, where we might expect an impf., a pres. injunc., or a pf. The two parallel y├йna clauses have perfects. Hoffmann does not comment on this usage.

The pf. ─Бpir├й in b takes the partitive gen. amс╣Ы╠Бtasya c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е in c. As in the other occurrences of this phrase (IX.70.2, 4, 110.4) with Geldner I take this as a reference to the heavenly soma, with the nominalized neut. amс╣Ы╠Бta- тАШ(drink) of immortalityтАЩ.

See comm. ad IX.70.2 and, on supposed masc. c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е, VIII.5.14. Renou supplies instead тАШprincipeтАЩ: тАЬau beau (principe) immortel.тАЭ This is the only finite med. form of the well-attested pf. to тИЪ─Бp, beside two occurrences of the part. K├╝mmel. (118) asserts that the medial forms have the тАЬinattingentтАЭ sense тАШhave successтАЩ (implicitly interpr. our form here without the partitive gen. obj.), but he does not cite this passage. Geldner (n. 4c) seems to suggest something of the same thing as an alternative, but making amс╣Ы╠Бtasya c─Б╠Бruс╣Зaс╕е dependent on sumn├й as he suggests does not seem to me to work. Although it might seem circular for the poets to acquire a share of (heavenly) soma through (earthly) soma, this is exactly the point also of IX.70.2. See comm. ad loc I cannot detect the semantic nuance between тИЪ─Бp тАШacquireтАЩ (─Бpir├й b) and тИЪ(n)a┼Ы тАШattainтАЩ (─Бna┼Ы├║с╕е d). In this passage the first has a more material object, the second an immaterial one, but this distribution does not hold elsewhere.

I take the pl. ┼Ыr├бvaс╣Гsi as distributive: each one of the pl. subj. acquires his own ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Vs. 4 is clearly syntactically dependent on vs. 3, with a series of three rel. cl. introduced by y├йna referring to Soma, the 2nd ps. subj. of 3.

By whom they won the fame of lovely Amrta in the felicity of Gods.

English translation:

тАЬThis (Soma) when effused flows most exhilarating through the woollen fleece, sporting like a wave of water.тАЭ

This most exhilarating one here, pressed in a stream, purifies himself with the fleeces of sheep,
playing like a wave of the waters, с│У

The 1st hemistich of vs. 6 is a relative cl. in the 3rd ps. dependent on vs. 5, also in the 3rd ps. The 2nd hemistich of 6 switches to 2nd ps.

Effused, he floweth in a stream, best rapture-giver, in the long wool of the sheep,
Sporting, as ’twere the waters’ wave.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou who by your might extricated from the rock the quick-moving kine abiding in the waters, you have spread out a pasturage for cattle and horses; like a mailed (warrior) slay (the asuras), brave (Soma).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Interpretation: Who by his might cut the quick-moving waters of the firmament from out of the cloud, you get a herd of cattle and horses

Jamison Brereton

He who with his might cut the ruddy, watery cows out from within the rock. You have extended your control over the enclosure of the cows and
horses. Like a man in armor, break into it, o bold one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner suggests that p─Бda a concerns the Vс╣Ыtra myth and b the Vala myth, based primarily on ├бpya- тАШwateryтАЩ as a descriptor of the cows in the former. This does not seem to me sufficient evidence, esp. because ├бpya- is not elsewhere used in connection with the Vс╣Ыtra myth. In his n. (6b) Geldner appears amenable to a unitary interpr. of ab, as only depicting the Vala myth, as I also take it, though why the cows are тАШwateryтАЩ isnтАЩt clear to me. GeldnerтАЩs alternative explanation, involving X.67.5, does not seem terribly strong. It suggest it may be connected with the waters used in the ritual preparation of soma; see vs. 7.

On abh├н тИЪtan see comm. ad VIII.6.25.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 1st hemistich of vs. 6 is a relative cl. in the 3rd ps. dependent on vs. 5, also in the 3rd ps. The 2nd hemistich of 6 switches to 2nd ps.

Griffith

He who from out the rocky cavern took with might the redmrefulgent watery Cows,
Thou masterest the stable full of kine and steeds: burst it, brave Lord, like one in mail.

Geldner

Der die Wasserk├╝he im Fels, der die K├╝he mit Kraft befreit hat - du hast einen Pferch von Rindern und Rossen eingehegt; erbrich ihn wie ein Geharnischter, du Mutiger!

Grassmann

Der aus dem Fels des Wassers rothe K├╝he du mit Kraft hervorgespalten hast, Du dehntest weit den Stall der Ross’ und Rinder aus schaff her sie, k├╝hner, wie ein Held.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPour forth (the Soma), sprinkle it round like a horse, adorable, dispenser of rain, dispenser of light, showerer of fluid, swimming in water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Press it, sprinkle it around, as one sprinkles a horseтАФ(the soma that is stoma, i.e.,) the praise song that crosses the waters, crosses the airy
realms,
that is howling in the wood and swimming in the waters,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains two sleight-of-hand manoeuvres. The first involves the simile and frame with p├бri с╣гi├▒cata тАШsprinkle aroundтАЩ. This verb ordinarily takes an acc. of the liquid sprinkled; see for ex. the immed. preceding hymn with the same lexeme: IX.107.1 p├бri тАж с╣гi├▒cata sut├бm тАЬsprinkle around the pressed (drink).тАЭ But the acc. in the simile, ├б┼Ыvaс╣Г n├б is the target of the sprinkling, not the liquid. So although the cases agree (implicitly: there is no expressed acc. in the frame), they have different syntactic functions (the opposite of my тАЬcase disharmonyтАЭ). So Geldner explicitly (n. 7a). For horses as obj. with тИЪsic, see IV.43.6 s├нndhur ha v─Бс╣Г ras├бy─Б si├▒cad ├б┼Ыv─Бn тАЬThe Sindhu River sprinkles your [=A┼ЫvinsтАЩ] horses with the Ras─Б.тАЭ The 2nd sleight of hand follows immediately. Both the verb and the string of acc. that follow demand the obj. *s├│mam, but instead we find the near rhyme form st├│mam тАШpraiseтАЩ. Rather than emend this to the easier reading (as Oldenberg seems inclined to do, along with numerous others; see his comm.), it is better to accept the implicit equation of the two ritual elements: the offered liquid and the offered words. This is not the only place in the RV where this trope is found.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Once again the 2nd vs. is syntactically dependent on the 1st in this prag─Бtha: 8ab is couched in the acc., continuing the acc. phrase in 7bc, and 8cd is a rel. cl. whose antecedent is the acc. phrase.

Griffith

Press ye and pour him, like a steed, laudworthy, speeding through the region and the flood,
Who swims in water, roan in wood;

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThousand-streamed, showererof benefits, augmenter of water, affectionate; (pour it forth) for the race of the gods which water-born is fostered by the water, the king, the god, the true, the great.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The bull of a thousand streams, growing strong through the milk, dear to the divine race,
who born of truth through truth has grown strong as king, god, and lofty truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On Soma as truth see IX.97.23, 107.15.

Who born in Law hath waxen mighty by the Law, King, God, and lofty Ordinance.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine (Soma) lord of viands, who are devoted to the gods, bestow upon us brilliant and abundant food; separate the mid-aerial receptacle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Illuminate lofty splendor and glory, o lord of refreshment, as you seek the gods, o god.
Unleash the middle bucket [=rain cloud].

Jamison Brereton Notes

The impv. did─лh├н in b is accented because it follows the p─Бda-init. complex voc. phrase ├нс╣гas pate. On the impv. and its twin d─лdih├н with switched quantity, see Oldenberg ad loc. The well-attested redupl. formation(s) to тИЪd─л, a perfect transitioning to a redupl. pres. (see, e.g., my тАЬThe Vedic Perfect ImperativeтАЭ [Fs. Lubotsky, 2018]: 58- 59), show a long ─л in the root syllable only in the impv. did─лh├н (1x accented, 11x unacc.); the weak forms otherwise show only d─лdi-, incl. the competing impv. d─лdih├н (1x accented, 17x unacc.). They are mostly distributed metrically: d─лdihi is found almost exclusively in final position in a Jagat─л or iambic dimeter line; did─лhi regularly takes final position in a Triс╣гс╣нubh line. But a few examples of both forms are found in metrically unfavorable places. E.g., in VIII.60.6 d─лdihi occurs after a 5-syl. opening; although HEAVY LIGHT is an attested break, LIGHT LIGHT (*didihi, to an unattested stem form) would be better. Likewise, our form, found after a 4-syl. opening, presents an unusual L H L break, though neither *d─лdihi nor *didihi would give the most favored break. (Oldenberg states that we would expect *d─лdihi here, but does not suggest emending because there are several other exx. of L H L breaks in this hymn.) It is also worth noting that did─лhi is found several times in the curious phrase тАж s├бm ├нс╣гo did─лhi (naс╕е)# тАЬilluminate our refreshments entirelyтАЭ (III.3.7, 54.22, V.4.2), and our passage contains the voc. ├нс╣гas pate тАЬo lord of refreshment,тАЭ so that the presence of ├нс╣гaс╕е may have triggered the did─лhi variant here. As for the source of the variation, itтАЩs possible that transposing the Jagat─л/iambic-final d─лdihi into a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence may have led to an almost mechanical balancing of quantities (on the model of alternations like vavardh- / v─Бvс╣Ыdh-), and then both forms were sometimes used outside of their original places (including did─лhi in Jagat─л/iambic cadences, with the addition of final naс╕е [III.3.7, V.25.2]), though this seems too convenient an explanation.

The notion that тАЬthe middle bucketтАЭ (k├│┼Ыa- madhyam├б-) is the rain cloud goes back to S─Бyaс╣Зa. and makes good sense, esp. given the explicit rain in the next vs. (10c).

It is possible that the impv. did─лh├н тАШilluminateтАЩ in the first hemistich is meant to evoke lightning in this context, although it is not otherwise found in this usage, as far as I can tell.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. are syntactically independent but linked by the theme of rain.

Griffith

Make splendid glory shine on us, thou Lord of strengthening food, God, as the Friend of Gods:
Unclose the fount of middle air.

Geldner

Leuchte du zu hohem Glanz und Ruhme, Herr der Labung, o Gott, nach den G├╢ttern verlangend! Entleere die mittlere Kufe!

Grassmann

O Herr des Trankes, strahle her, die G├╢tter liebend, Gut und grossen Glanz, o Gott, Den mittlern Schlauch er├╢ffne uns.

English translation:

тАЬCome, powerful (Soma) effused into the cups, like a prince the sustainer of the people; pour the course of the waters, the rain fromheaven; accomplish the rites for the worshipper who seeks cattle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Into the cups: adhi┼Ыavana phalak─Бyaс╕е, in the plural nks of the press

Jamison Brereton

Coil yourself into the two cups when you are pressed, skillful one, as the clanlord of the clans, like a draft-horse.
Purify yourself into the rain from heaven, the streaming of waters.
Quicken our insights for the quest for cattle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this usage of ─Б╠БтИЪva├▒c see comm. ad IX.2.2. This same phrase ─Б╠Б vacyasva (тАж) camv├▓с╕е is found in IX.97.2.

I take vi┼Ы─Б╠Бm тАж vi┼Ыp├бtiс╕е to be a syntagm like gaс╣З─Б╠Бn─Бm тАж gaс╣З├бpatim тАЬtrooplord of troopsтАЭ (II.23.1), with the simile v├бhnir n├б interposed. The expression in II.23.1 also has an interposed word, though just a Wackernagel enclitic tv─Б. Geldner takes the vi┼Ы- words as part of the simile, тАЬwie ein zu Wagen fahrender Clanf├╝rstтАЭ (and folds the gen. pl. vi┼Ы─Б╠Бm into its headnoun). He suggests an alternative (n. 10b) closer to mine, though again with the gen. elided: тАЬwie ein Wagenross, du der Clanf├╝rst.тАЭ And, with the aid of parentheses, Renou gets three separate NPs out of it: тАЬtel un chef de clan, (ma├оtre) des clans, conducteur (du char).тАЭ The syntagms vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├нm div├бс╕е тАж r─лt├нm ap─Б╠Бm exactly replicate the problematic compds vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├н-dy─Бvo r─лty-─Б╠Аpaс╕е in nearby IX.106.8. See comm. there. Whether there is any direct functional relationship between the cmpds and the syntagms, the two sequences must be considered together.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHim have they milked from heaven, the shedder of exhilarating juice, the thousand-streamed, the showerer (of benefits), bearing all treasures.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They have milked out of the heavens this thousand-streamed bull, who arouses exhilaration,
who brings all good things.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The accentuation of d├нvaс╕е poses problems. Pace Geldner (n. 11b), who considers d├нvaс╕е a gen. sg. with unusual accent, I take it as acc. pl. (flg. Oldenberg, in turn fld. by Renou and L├╝ders 202). Given the correctly accented gen./abl. sg. div├бс╕е in the immediately preceding vs. (10c), it is hard to believe that the poet would get the accent wrong, esp. in this exceptionally common form. As Oldenberg suggests, тИЪduh takes a double acc. here. On d├нvaс╕е as acc. pl., see also AiG III.226-27.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. are syntactically independent but both concern Soma as bull (vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б- 11b, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- 12a).

They have drained him the Steer of heaven, him with a thousand streams, distilling rapturous joy,
Him who brings all things excellent.

Eben diesen rauscherregten tausendstrahligen Bullen des Himmels haben sie gemolken, der alle Sch├дtze bringt.

Grassmann

Sie molken diesen Himmelsstier, der Rausch erregt und der in tausend Str├╢men fliesst, Den alle G├╝ter tragenden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe showerer (of benefits) is manifested begetting (light) immortal, destroying the darkness with (his) radiance; glorified by the wise he has assumed his shining robe; the triple (oblation is supported) by his act.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He has assumed his shining robe: he has blended himself with the milk, for the sake of being cleansed

Jamison Brereton

The bull has been born, the immortal that gives birth, burning away the darkness with his light.
Well-praised by the poets, he dons his raiment, a threefold one, by his wondrous ability.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the тАЬthreefoldтАЭ (tridh─Б╠Бtu) nature of SomaтАЩs clothing, see comm. ad IX.70.8.

by whom we will bring Mitra and Varuс╣Зa here and Indra here for

Jamison Brereton Notes

The nom., acc., voc., and gen. pl. of mar├║t- do not fit any standard RVic cadence. It is not surprising then that though instr. mar├║dbhiс╕е and dat./abl.

mar├║dbhyaс╕е are regularly found in cadences, the other forms are almost entirely absent. P─Бda b has a nom. pl. in the cadence (made worse by the fact that the word is preceded by a light syllable, (y├б)sya. VII.32.10 has the same sequence, also in a double y├бsya construction. Most of the few other cadential forms are found in dimeter vs. (e.g., VIII.3.21, VIII.7.30).

For Indra to drink, o SomaтАФheld by men, having good weapons and most exhilarating,
purify yourself as the most honeyed.

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдХрд░реНрдордпреЛрдЧреА рдХреЗ (рд╣рд╛рд░реНрджрд┐) рд╣реГрджрдпрд░реВрдк (рд╕реЛрдордзрд╛рдирдореН) рдЕрдиреНрддрдГрдХрд░рдг рдХреЛ (рдЖрд╡рд┐рд╢) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдВ, (рдЗрд╡) рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡рдГ) рдирджрд┐рдпреЗрдВ (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдореН) рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рдЗрд╕реА рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╣рдорд╛рд░реА рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдпреЗрдВ рдЖрдкрдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдВ, рдЖрдк (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдп) рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдФрд░ (рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛рдп) рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП (рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡реЗ) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпреЛрдЧреА рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЬреБрд╖реНрдЯрдГ) рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЖрдк (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХ рдХрд╛ (рдЙрддреНрддрдордГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрд░рд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдореНрднрдГ) рд╕рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╣реИрдВ реерезремрее

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдХреЛрдЯрд┐-рдХреЛрдЯрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдб рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдЖрдзрд╛рд░ рдкрд░ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░ рд╣реИрдВ рдФрд░ рдЬреЛ рдХрд░реНрдордпреЛрдЧреА рддрдерд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпреЛрдЧреА рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдпреЛрдЧреА рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣реА рдПрдХрдорд╛рддреНрд░ рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕реНрдп рджреЗрд╡ рд╣реИ реерезремрее рдпрд╣ резрежрео рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ резреп рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖрее

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН !
